### Post by archolman on 2011-06-15

I have just replaced a Hard Drive, & had to reinstall XP & 10.04.2LTS from scratch, (it was a TOTAL failure)
The system now will not boot into XP, or either of the 2 Linux kernels or the recovery modes, without several attempts.
( I'm using a LiveCD now.)
POST is good.

GRUB loads, but when I select an OS, it powers off. Windows shows the splash for a few seconds, then shuts down.
Yesterday, I was able to boot into Linux after booting into Windows, but today Windows won't boot either.

On examining the GRUB menu (e) the first line in the Linux records is 'recordfail'
 I will attempt to boot from HDD now, & post the GRUB output here.


EDIT: If I run MEMTEST first, up to Test6, it boots normally. Any advise please?

### Post by oldfred on 2011-06-15
This will show entire boot configuration. If you can boot you can run it from your Ubuntu install or from a LiveCD:

Boot Info Script courtesy of forum members meierfra & Gert Hulselmans
Page with instructions and download:
[http://bootinfoscript.sourceforge.net/](http://bootinfoscript.sourceforge.net/)
Paste results.txt in a New Reply, then highlight entire file and click on # in edit panel(code tags) to make it easier to read.
Or You can generate the tags first by pressing the # icon in the New Reply Edit toolbar and then paste the contents between the generated [ code] paste here [ /code] tags.
V60 has improved formating and requires code tags to make it legible. New Version is a zip file that you have to extract to get .sh to run.

---

# DO NOT EDIT THIS FILE

### BEGIN /etc/grub.d/00_header ###
if [ -s $prefix/grubenv ]; then
  load_env
fi
set default="0"
if [ ${prev_saved_entry} ]; then
  set saved_entry=${prev_saved_entry}
  save_env saved_entry
  set prev_saved_entry=
  save_env prev_saved_entry
  set boot_once=true
fi

function savedefault {
  if [ -z ${boot_once} ]; then
    saved_entry=${chosen}
    save_env saved_entry
  fi
}

function recordfail {
  set recordfail=1
  if [ -n ${have_grubenv} ]; then if [ -z ${boot_once} ]; then save_env recordfail; fi; fi
}
insmod ext2
set root='(hd0,5)'
search --no-floppy --fs-uuid --set 3e53a3b4-598b-4cb7-8ea3-f9c25dd382c1
if loadfont /usr/share/grub/unicode.pf2 ; then
  set gfxmode=640x480
  insmod gfxterm
  insmod vbe
  if terminal_output gfxterm ; then true ; else
    # For backward compatibility with versions of terminal.mod that don't
    # understand terminal_output
    terminal gfxterm
  fi
fi
insmod ext2
set root='(hd0,5)'
search --no-floppy --fs-uuid --set 3e53a3b4-598b-4cb7-8ea3-f9c25dd382c1
set locale_dir=($root)/boot/grub/locale
set lang=en
insmod gettext
if [ ${recordfail} = 1 ]; then
  set timeout=-1
else
  set timeout=10
fi
### END /etc/grub.d/00_header ###

### Post by oldfred on 2011-06-15
Boot script looks normal to me. 

Is this an older system with a much larger hard drive? Did you change from IDE to SATA? Windows XP requires drivers for SATA and for AHCI, but you can set BIOS for IDE mode.

Old BIOS, new drive 137GB max boot size
NTFS partition needs chkdsk, gparted will not see drive if chkdsk flag set, flag is set on resize

I have not installed the AHCI drivers.
SATA mode should stay in AHCI unless you are getting nasty issues (which shouldn't happen with linux or vista/win7). The main reason why people change SATA mode to 'compatibility' is because winXP wont work with AHCI without loading the drivers..and you need a floppy drive to load the drivers, which most newer computers don't have (and lots of people are lazy anyway).

Did you resize windows on install? It might need fixboot and/or chkdsk, but script is not showing a problem. These are all the repairs I know but you should not need them all especially on a new install.
Description of the Windows XP Recovery Console for advanced users list of commands
[http://support.microsoft.com/kb/314058/](http://support.microsoft.com/kb/314058/)
FIXMBR  C:  #do not run if you still want grub in the MBR
FIXBOOT  C:
BOOTCFG  /rebuild  # rebuilds boot.ini
chkdsk c: /r

COPY [CDDRIVE]:\I386\NTLDR  C:\
COPY [CDDRIVE]:\I386\NTDETECT.COM  C:\

---

### Post by archolman on 2011-06-15
The system was home-built 4years ago with a CCLOnline MB bundle, with dual-boot & SATA considered from the start, for music & multi-media production in Linux & Windows. I used a (smaller) refurbished SATA drive from the start.
PS was new.
The board is an ABIT NF-M2SV AM2 Socket, with a 3GB/sec SATA rate.
I've kept the BIOS updated.

The case & switches are a older than that, could it be a switch problem?  I can't see how, & it's odd that the thing will boot after a few minutes running a LiveCD or XP, almost as if it's temperature or time-dependent. :???:

---

### Post by oldfred on 2011-06-15
It might be a BIOS setting.

Have you checked log files to see if you have issues on any device? System, Administration, Log File Viewer?

Are you able to shutdown normally or not? Sometimes after abnormal shutdown, then you may have issues rebooting.
